class \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1Halfspace}{Halfspace}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Half Space\+: this is equivalent to the Planed in O\+DE. The separation plane is defined as n $\ast$ x = d. Points in the negative side of the separation plane (i.\+e. \{x $\vert$ n $\ast$ x $<$ d\}) are inside the half space and points in the positive side of the separation plane (i.\+e. \{x $\vert$ n $\ast$ x $>$ d\}) are outside the half space. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

class \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1InterpMotion}{Interp\+Motion}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Linear interpolation motion Each Motion is assumed to have constant linear velocity and angular velocity The motion is R(t)(p -\/ p\+\_\+ref) + p\+\_\+ref + T(t) Therefore, R(0) = R0, R(1) = R1 T(0) = T0 + R0 p\+\_\+ref -\/ p\+\_\+ref T(1) = T1 + R1 p\+\_\+ref -\/ p\+\_\+ref. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

class \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1KDOP}{K\+D\+OP}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1KDOP}{K\+D\+OP}} class describes the \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1KDOP}{K\+D\+OP}} collision structures. K is set as the template parameter, which should be 16, 18, or 24 The \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1KDOP}{K\+D\+OP}} structure is defined by some pairs of parallel planes defined by some axes. For K = 16, the planes are 6 \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1AABB}{A\+A\+BB}} planes and 10 diagonal planes that cut off some space of the edges\+: (-\/1,0,0) and (1,0,0) -\/$>$ indices 0 and 8 (0,-\/1,0) and (0,1,0) -\/$>$ indices 1 and 9 (0,0,-\/1) and (0,0,1) -\/$>$ indices 2 and 10 (-\/1,-\/1,0) and (1,1,0) -\/$>$ indices 3 and 11 (-\/1,0,-\/1) and (1,0,1) -\/$>$ indices 4 and 12 (0,-\/1,-\/1) and (0,1,1) -\/$>$ indices 5 and 13 (-\/1,1,0) and (1,-\/1,0) -\/$>$ indices 6 and 14 (-\/1,0,1) and (1,0,-\/1) -\/$>$ indices 7 and 15 For K = 18, the planes are 6 \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1AABB}{A\+A\+BB}} planes and 12 diagonal planes that cut off some space of the edges\+: (-\/1,0,0) and (1,0,0) -\/$>$ indices 0 and 9 (0,-\/1,0) and (0,1,0) -\/$>$ indices 1 and 10 (0,0,-\/1) and (0,0,1) -\/$>$ indices 2 and 11 (-\/1,-\/1,0) and (1,1,0) -\/$>$ indices 3 and 12 (-\/1,0,-\/1) and (1,0,1) -\/$>$ indices 4 and 13 (0,-\/1,-\/1) and (0,1,1) -\/$>$ indices 5 and 14 (-\/1,1,0) and (1,-\/1,0) -\/$>$ indices 6 and 15 (-\/1,0,1) and (1,0,-\/1) -\/$>$ indices 7 and 16 (0,-\/1,1) and (0,1,-\/1) -\/$>$ indices 8 and 17 For K = 18, the planes are 6 \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1AABB}{A\+A\+BB}} planes and 18 diagonal planes that cut off some space of the edges\+: (-\/1,0,0) and (1,0,0) -\/$>$ indices 0 and 12 (0,-\/1,0) and (0,1,0) -\/$>$ indices 1 and 13 (0,0,-\/1) and (0,0,1) -\/$>$ indices 2 and 14 (-\/1,-\/1,0) and (1,1,0) -\/$>$ indices 3 and 15 (-\/1,0,-\/1) and (1,0,1) -\/$>$ indices 4 and 16 (0,-\/1,-\/1) and (0,1,1) -\/$>$ indices 5 and 17 (-\/1,1,0) and (1,-\/1,0) -\/$>$ indices 6 and 18 (-\/1,0,1) and (1,0,-\/1) -\/$>$ indices 7 and 19 (0,-\/1,1) and (0,1,-\/1) -\/$>$ indices 8 and 20 (-\/1, -\/1, 1) and (1, 1, -\/1) -\/-\/$>$ indices 9 and 21 (-\/1, 1, -\/1) and (1, -\/1, 1) -\/-\/$>$ indices 10 and 22 (1, -\/1, -\/1) and (-\/1, 1, 1) -\/-\/$>$ indices 11 and 23. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

struct \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1TBVMotionBoundVisitorVisitImpl_3_01S_00_01RSS_3_01S_01_4_00_01InterpMotion_3_01S_01_4_01_4}{T\+B\+V\+Motion\+Bound\+Visitor\+Visit\+Impl$<$ S, R\+S\+S$<$ S $>$, Interp\+Motion$<$ S $>$ $>$}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Compute the motion bound for a bounding volume along a given direction n according to mu $<$ $\vert$v $\ast$ n$\vert$ + $\vert$$\vert$w x n$\vert$$\vert$(r + max($\vert$$\vert$ci$\ast$$\vert$$\vert$)) where $\vert$$\vert$ci$\ast$$\vert$$\vert$ = $\vert$$\vert$\+R0(ci) x w$\vert$$\vert$. w is the angular axis (normalized) and ci are the endpoints of the generator primitives of \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1RSS}{R\+SS}}. Notice that all bv parameters are in the local frame of the object, but n should be in the global frame (the reason is that the motion (t1, t2 and t) is in global frame) \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
struct \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1TBVMotionBoundVisitorVisitImpl_3_01S_00_01RSS_3_01S_01_4_00_01ScrewMotion_3_01S_01_4_01_4}{T\+B\+V\+Motion\+Bound\+Visitor\+Visit\+Impl$<$ S, R\+S\+S$<$ S $>$, Screw\+Motion$<$ S $>$ $>$}}
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Compute the motion bound for a bounding volume along a given direction n according to mu $<$ $\vert$v $\ast$ n$\vert$ + $\vert$$\vert$w x n$\vert$$\vert$(r + max($\vert$$\vert$ci$\ast$$\vert$$\vert$)) where $\vert$$\vert$ci$\ast$$\vert$$\vert$ = $\vert$$\vert$\+R0(ci) x w$\vert$$\vert$. w is the angular axis (normalized) and ci are the endpoints of the generator primitives of \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1RSS}{R\+SS}}. Notice that all bv parameters are in the local frame of the object, but n should be in the global frame (the reason is that the motion (t1, t2 and t) is in global frame) \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Compute the motion bound for a triangle along a given direction n according to mu $<$ $\vert$v $\ast$ n$\vert$ + $\vert$$\vert$w x n$\vert$$\vert$(max$\vert$$\vert$ci$\ast$$\vert$$\vert$) where $\vert$$\vert$ci$\ast$$\vert$$\vert$ = $\vert$$\vert$\+R0(ci) x w$\vert$$\vert$ / $|$w$|$. w is the angular velocity and ci are the triangle vertex coordinates. Notice that the triangle is in the local frame of the object, but n should be in the global frame (the reason is that the motion (t1, t2 and t) is in global frame) \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

{\footnotesize template$<$typename S $>$ }\\void \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacefcl_a57e2f598067b3c530f335b1ddcd84691}{seg\+Coords}} (S \&t, S \&u, S a, S b, S A\+\_\+dot\+\_\+B, S A\+\_\+dot\+\_\+T, S B\+\_\+dot\+\_\+T)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Finds the parameters t \& u corresponding to the two closest points on a pair of line segments. The first segment is defined as Pa + A$\ast$t, 0 $<$= t $<$= a, where \char`\"{}\+Pa\char`\"{} is one endpoint of the segment, \char`\"{}\+A\char`\"{} is a unit vector pointing to the other endpoint, and t is a scalar that produces all the points between the two endpoints. Since \char`\"{}\+A\char`\"{} is a unit vector, \char`\"{}a\char`\"{} is the segment\textquotesingle{}s length. The second segment is defined as Pb + B$\ast$u, 0 $<$= u $<$= b. Many of the terms needed by the algorithm are already computed for other purposes,so we just pass these terms into the function instead of complete specifications of each segment. \char`\"{}\+T\char`\"{} in the dot products is the vector betweeen Pa and Pb. Reference\+: \char`\"{}\+On fast computation of distance between line segments.\char`\"{} Vladimir J. Lumelsky, in Information Processing Letters, no. 21, pages 55-\/61, 1985. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacefcl_af2fe840c8fff391c44a7dee91f23fc1b}\label{namespacefcl_af2fe840c8fff391c44a7dee91f23fc1b}} 
{\footnotesize template$<$typename S $>$ }\\bool \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacefcl_af2fe840c8fff391c44a7dee91f23fc1b}{in\+Voronoi}} (S a, S b, S Anorm\+\_\+dot\+\_\+B, S Anorm\+\_\+dot\+\_\+T, S A\+\_\+dot\+\_\+B, S A\+\_\+dot\+\_\+T, S B\+\_\+dot\+\_\+T)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Returns whether the nearest point on rectangle edge Pb + B$\ast$u, 0 $<$= u $<$= b, to the rectangle edge, Pa + A$\ast$t, 0 $<$= t $<$= a, is within the half space determined by the point Pa and the direction Anorm. A,B, and Anorm are unit vectors. T is the vector between Pa and Pb. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacefcl_abc34e21d3f9962e5f53eb9c0c07911e5}\label{namespacefcl_abc34e21d3f9962e5f53eb9c0c07911e5}}

\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Distance between two oriented rectangles; P and Q (optional return values) are the closest points in the rectangles, both are in the local frame of the first rectangle. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

{\footnotesize template$<$typename S , typename DerivedA , typename DerivedB $>$ }\\S \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacefcl_af376c74ad0f6c51b62de474d261a99b5}{distance}} (const Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base$<$ DerivedA $>$ \&R0, const Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base$<$ DerivedB $>$ \&T0, const \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1RSS}{R\+SS}}$<$ S $>$ \&b1, const \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1RSS}{R\+SS}}$<$ S $>$ \&b2, Vector3$<$ S $>$ $\ast$P, Vector3$<$ S $>$ $\ast$Q)

{\footnotesize template$<$typename S $>$ }\\F\+C\+L\+\_\+\+E\+X\+P\+O\+RT std\+::size\+\_\+t \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacefcl_a3385ed4bd726ea11628795d8591878ed}{collide}} (const \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1CollisionObject}{Collision\+Object}}$<$ S $>$ $\ast$o1, const \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1CollisionObject}{Collision\+Object}}$<$ S $>$ $\ast$o2, const \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1CollisionRequest}{Collision\+Request}}$<$ S $>$ \&request, \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1CollisionResult}{Collision\+Result}}$<$ S $>$ \&result)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Main collision interface\+: given two collision objects, and the requirements for contacts, including num of max contacts, whether perform exhaustive collision (i.\+e., returning returning all the contact points), whether return detailed contact information (i.\+e., normal, contact point, depth; otherwise only contact primitive id is returned), this function performs the collision between them. Return value is the number of contacts generated between the two objects. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
Main namespace. 

collision and distance function on traversal nodes. these functions provide a higher level abstraction for collision functions provided in collision\+\_\+func\+\_\+matrix

\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacefcl_ab34a6100f661c140087228266ee246d0}\label{namespacefcl_ab34a6100f661c140087228266ee246d0}} 
\index{fcl@{fcl}!DefaultCollisionFunction@{DefaultCollisionFunction}}
\index{DefaultCollisionFunction@{DefaultCollisionFunction}!fcl@{fcl}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DefaultCollisionFunction()}{DefaultCollisionFunction()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename S $>$ \\
bool fcl\+::\+Default\+Collision\+Function (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1CollisionObject}{Collision\+Object}}$<$ S $>$ $\ast$}]{o1,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1CollisionObject}{Collision\+Object}}$<$ S $>$ $\ast$}]{o2,  }\item[{void $\ast$}]{data }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Provides a simple callback for the collision query in the \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1BroadPhaseCollisionManager}{Broad\+Phase\+Collision\+Manager}}. It assumes the {\ttfamily data} parameter is non-\/null and points to an instance of \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultCollisionData}{Default\+Collision\+Data}}. It simply invokes the {\ttfamily collide()} method on the culled pair of geometries and stores the results in the data\textquotesingle{}s \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1CollisionResult}{Collision\+Result}} instance. 

This callback will cause the broadphase evaluation to stop if\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item the collision requests {\itshape disables} cost {\itshape and}
\item the collide() reports a collision for the culled pair, {\itshape and}
\item we\textquotesingle{}ve reported the number of contacts requested in the \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1CollisionRequest}{Collision\+Request}}.
\end{DoxyItemize}

For a given instance of \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultCollisionData}{Default\+Collision\+Data}}, if broadphase evaluation has already terminated (i.\+e., \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacefcl_ab34a6100f661c140087228266ee246d0}{Default\+Collision\+Function()}} returned {\ttfamily true}), subsequent invocations with the same instance of \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultCollisionData}{Default\+Collision\+Data}} will return immediately, requesting termination of broadphase evaluation (i.\+e., return {\ttfamily true}).


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em o1} & The first object in the culled pair. \\
\hline
{\em o2} & The second object in the culled pair. \\
\hline
{\em data} & A non-\/null pointer to a \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultCollisionData}{Default\+Collision\+Data}} instance. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
{\ttfamily true} if the broadphase evaluation should stop. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em S} & The scalar type with which the computation will be performed. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacefcl_ad2fadb29fbd400534e9ef6b9bf7116af}\label{namespacefcl_ad2fadb29fbd400534e9ef6b9bf7116af}} 
\index{fcl@{fcl}!DefaultContinuousCollisionFunction@{DefaultContinuousCollisionFunction}}
\index{DefaultContinuousCollisionFunction@{DefaultContinuousCollisionFunction}!fcl@{fcl}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DefaultContinuousCollisionFunction()}{DefaultContinuousCollisionFunction()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename S $>$ \\
bool fcl\+::\+Default\+Continuous\+Collision\+Function (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1ContinuousCollisionObject}{Continuous\+Collision\+Object}}$<$ S $>$ $\ast$}]{o1,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1ContinuousCollisionObject}{Continuous\+Collision\+Object}}$<$ S $>$ $\ast$}]{o2,  }\item[{void $\ast$}]{data }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Provides a simple callback for the continuous collision query in the \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1BroadPhaseCollisionManager}{Broad\+Phase\+Collision\+Manager}}. It assumes the {\ttfamily data} parameter is non-\/null and points to an instance of \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultContinuousCollisionData}{Default\+Continuous\+Collision\+Data}}. It simply invokes the {\ttfamily collide()} method on the culled pair of geometries and stores the results in the data\textquotesingle{}s \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1ContinuousCollisionResult}{Continuous\+Collision\+Result}} instance. 

This callback will never cause the broadphase evaluation to terminate early. However, if the {\ttfamily done} member of the \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultContinuousCollisionData}{Default\+Continuous\+Collision\+Data}} is set to true, this method will simply return without doing any computation.

For a given instance of \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultContinuousCollisionData}{Default\+Continuous\+Collision\+Data}}, if broadphase evaluation has already terminated (i.\+e., \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacefcl_ad2fadb29fbd400534e9ef6b9bf7116af}{Default\+Continuous\+Collision\+Function()}} returned {\ttfamily true}), subsequent invocations with the same instance of \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultCollisionData}{Default\+Collision\+Data}} will return immediately, requesting termination of broadphase evaluation (i.\+e., return {\ttfamily true}).


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em o1} & The first object in the culled pair. \\
\hline
{\em o2} & The second object in the culled pair. \\
\hline
{\em data} & A non-\/null pointer to a \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultCollisionData}{Default\+Collision\+Data}} instance. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
True if the broadphase evaluation should stop. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em S} & The scalar type with which the computation will be performed. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{namespacefcl_a9dd1a4a61b0a173758d83df5593241f8}\label{namespacefcl_a9dd1a4a61b0a173758d83df5593241f8}} 
\index{fcl@{fcl}!DefaultDistanceFunction@{DefaultDistanceFunction}}
\index{DefaultDistanceFunction@{DefaultDistanceFunction}!fcl@{fcl}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DefaultDistanceFunction()}{DefaultDistanceFunction()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename S $>$ \\
bool fcl\+::\+Default\+Distance\+Function (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1CollisionObject}{Collision\+Object}}$<$ S $>$ $\ast$}]{o1,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1CollisionObject}{Collision\+Object}}$<$ S $>$ $\ast$}]{o2,  }\item[{void $\ast$}]{data,  }\item[{S \&}]{dist }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Provides a simple callback for the distance query in the \mbox{\hyperlink{classfcl_1_1BroadPhaseCollisionManager}{Broad\+Phase\+Collision\+Manager}}. It assumes the {\ttfamily data} parameter is non-\/null and points to an instance of \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultDistanceData}{Default\+Distance\+Data}}. It simply invokes the {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacefcl_a96484159054b342a432d5a861c3723f1}{distance()}}} method on the culled pair of geometries and stores the results in the data\textquotesingle{}s \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DistanceResult}{Distance\+Result}} instance. 

This callback will cause the broadphase evaluation to stop if\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item The distance is less than or equal to zero (i.\+e., the pair is in contact).
\end{DoxyItemize}

For a given instance of \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultDistanceData}{Default\+Distance\+Data}}, if broadphase evaluation has already terminated (i.\+e., \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacefcl_a9dd1a4a61b0a173758d83df5593241f8}{Default\+Distance\+Function()}} returned {\ttfamily true}), subsequent invocations with the same instance of \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultDistanceData}{Default\+Distance\+Data}} will simply report the previously reported minimum distance and request termination of broadphase evaluation (i.\+e., return {\ttfamily true}).


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em o1} & The first object in the culled pair. \\
\hline
{\em o2} & The second object in the culled pair. \\
\hline
{\em data} & A non-\/null pointer to a \mbox{\hyperlink{structfcl_1_1DefaultDistanceData}{Default\+Distance\+Data}} instance. \\
\hline
{\em dist} & The distance computed by \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacefcl_a96484159054b342a432d5a861c3723f1}{distance()}}. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
{\ttfamily true} if the broadphase evaluation should stop. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\hline
